Natick Finance Committee
October 7, 2025
Greetings to all Town Meeting Members, Taxpayers, and Residents of Natick,
The Natick Finance Committee’s recommendations for articles appearing on the warrant for the
2025 Fall Annual Town Meeting are enclosed.
Under the Town’s Charter, the Finance Committee is required to hold public hearings
on the Town Administrator’s proposed budget for each Town agency and “昀椀le a
report containing its recommendations for actions on the proposed budget” (Natick
Home Rule Charter Article 5 Section 6).
Under the Town’s By-Laws, the Finance Committee is also required to “consider all
matters of business included within the articles of any warrant for a Town Meeting,
and shall, after due consideration, report thereon, in print, its recommendation as to
each article” (Natick By-Laws, Chapter 23, Section 4).  
In the Fall of 2025, the Finance Committee met of the following dates: 8/28, 9/11, 9/16, 9/18, 
9/25, 9/30, and 10/7. The Capital subcommittee also held meetings on 9/16 and 9/25 (minutes 
approval only).
Please consult the Town’s “Town Meeting Information” webpage for additional info and 
updates:  
https://natickma.gov/375/Town-Meeting-Information
Please also visit the Finance Committee’s Town Meeting Member Resource website, which will
be updated throughout Fall Town Meeting for late breaking information, new and 
supplementary information, videos, etc:  https://sites.google.com/natickma.org/昀椀ncom
The Finance Committee’s Fall Annual Recommendation Book will be available shortly and 
will be mailed to each Town Meeting Member once printed. 
Our recommendations are respectfully submitted for your consideration.
Natick Finance Committee,
Todd Gillenwater, Chair Richard Pope, Vice Chair Cody Jacobs, Secretary
Hossam Behery Leona Bessonova Dirk Coburn

TOWN ADMINISTRATION 
   
JAMES ERRICKSON ◆ T own Administrator 
jerrickson@natickma.org ◆ (508) 647-6410 
13 East Central St. Natick, MA 01760 ◆ 
www.natickma.gov 
 
 
October 3, 2025 
 
RE: T own Administrator’s Letter to T own Meeting - 2025 Fall Annual T own Meeting 
 
Dear Town Meeting Members, 
 
I am honored to provide this message to the 2025 Fall Annual Town Meeting. The Town 
Administration team has been busy these past several months advancing our core values  
- We Welcome, We Listen, We Lead -  throughout the organization in order to provide high 
quality services to the Natick Community. Since April, we’ve advanced numerous 
initiatives, welcomed new and said goodbye to members of the team (a few highlighted 
below), and continued to improve overall engagement within the community and 
organization.  
 
To highlight a few: 
 
Former Johnson Elementary School Reuse Engagement -  Starting in April 2025, Town 
Administration and the Select Board embarked on a 2+ year community engagement 
process designed to inform an eventual Select Board decision on the future reuse of the 
former Johnson Elementary School property. The Select Board has held monthly Johnson 
Speak opportunities at Select Board meetings, multiple <oüce hours= at the Johnson 
School site, a walking tour of the property, and conducted numerous surveys, all designed 
to provide a multitude of engagement opportunities for the public to help inform the 
future of the property. A public forum is planned for October 6th designed to ideate 
potential scenarios (ie. future uses) and reﬁne a scope to inform next steps in the process.  
 
Stay informed and sign up to receive project updates by visiting: 
https://www.natickma.gov/2113/PROJECT-Johnson-Future-Use 
 
NEW! Deputy T own Administrator - Director of Finance - Ari Sky - This fall, the Natick 
team welcomed Ari Sky as our new Deputy Town Administrator - Director of Finance. Ari 
brings several decades of municipal ﬁnance and management experience, including the 
past 10+ years in Massachusetts communities. Hailing originally from Portland Maine, Ari 
will be leading the Finance Department - assessors, comptroller, collector/treasurer, and 
budgeting - continuing to advance the many initiatives that support the Town’s AAA Bond 
ratings and strong ﬁnancials.  
 
Ari joins Natick due to the retirement of John Townsend, following his 8 years of service 
to the community. Thank you to John for his leadership and commitment to Natick.  
 
 
 
5

--- Page 10 ---

Thank you Dave Moores for your 40+ years of service  to Natick - The Town bid adieu to 
Dave Moores who retired this October after 40+ years of service to the community. Natick 
born and raised, Dave started working for the Town as a custodian while a student at 
Natick High. Through the years, Dave held many jobs within the Facilities Department, 
eventually taking on the leadership role of Facilities Maintenance Manager.  As a valued 
member of the team, Dave was a trusted resource for all who worked for and with him. 
Though we trust Dave will have a great time in retirement, we hope he returns to say hi to 
his Natick family. 
 
New Growth and Free Cash - Natick experienced a new growth ﬁgure this fall that 
exceeded budget expectations, led by a strong residential market and robust commercial 
investment. Budgeted for $1.1 million for FY 2026, New Growth came in just over 
approximately $2 million. Town Meeting will be asked to appropriate the additional 
revenue (approx $900k) to fund Operational and Capital Stabilization accounts, 
continuing our priority of rebuilding stabilization funds post pandemic. 
 
As of Town Meeting, the Town’s certiﬁed Free Cash number is pending review by the 
State’s Department of Revenue (DOR). Depending on the Free Cash certiﬁcation amount, 
Town Administration intends to seek Town Meeting authorization to utilize these funds to 
support three primary objectives:  
 
● Supplement the Capital Improvement Program 
● Invest in stabilization accounts (General, Operational, and/or Capital) 
● Preserve a balance for consideration/use as part of the FY 2027 budget 
 
Budget considerations for FY27 - as we enter the budgeting season for FY27, a myriad of 
items are being monitored by staﬀ. The Town is greatly appreciative and beneﬁting from 
the passage of the $7M override this past Spring supported by the voters. With that said, 
the items inûuencing the Town’s budget are expected to have a greater impact in the 
coming years that even current revenue increases (limited by Proposition 2½) can sustain, 
leading to the continued need to be ﬁscally conservative with our resources.  
 
Items of particular concern include: 
 
● Impacts from Federal policy & funding decisions 
● State Aid realities 
● Capital Improvement Program (CIP) costs - increased substantially in the past 5 
years (example - vehicles up nearly 50% since 2019/2020) 
● Health Insurance Costs - expected to increase signiﬁcantly in the coming year+ as 
the  health care system feels the stresses of Federal & State policies/funding 
● Property & Liability Insurance - expected to increase above typical in the coming 
year+ as the insurance industry grapples with increased costs due to disasters 
around the country  
 
Zoning, ADUs, & MBTA Communities – Town Meeting is being asked to consider a 
number of zoning bylaw amendments (Articles 20 – 29) designed to both modernize the 
Town’s zoning bylaws (an ongoing, multi-year initiative) and advance initiatives that 
support targeted new growth opportunities, particularly in the areas proximate to Natick’s 
 
6

--- Page 11 ---

Commuter Rail stations and core business districts. Through the tireless and dedicated 
work of Amanda Loomis, Community and Economic Development (CED) Director, 
members of the CED team, and the Planning Board, these zoning amendments are highly 
technical, thoughtful, inclusive of extensive community/business engagement, and 
well-drafted. I urge members of the community to research the materials available to be 
informed about these important articles being considered by Town Meeting.  
 
Resources are available on the CED Website: 
https://www.natickma.gov/162/Community-Economic-Development 
 
In closing, I want to thank all of our talented Town Staﬀ, engaged volunteers, and elected/ 
appointed oücials for their continued support and dedication to the Natick community.  
 
Very truly yours, 
 
 
James Errickson 
Town Administrator

Budget Overview:
The Town assumes debt to finance many capital projects. Natick’s debt is funded through bond issues. The
Town can only issue new debt with the approval of two-thirds of Town Meeting.
Debt service includes general fund principal and interest payments for both exempt and non-exempt debt,
as well as temporary borrowing. Also included in these figures are debt issuance costs and leased
equipment costs.
Debt is the main financing tool municipalities use to continually replace and maintain their capital
infrastructure. As such, it is important to monitor how much debt the community has at any one time and
to determine the impact that debt service has on the operating budget and taxpayers. Credit rating
agencies monitor the amount of debt a community carries, just as they evaluate individual credit. They
consider factors such as the debt-to-revenue ratio and the level of debt service per capita and per
household.
Natick’ s Debt P erformance
FY25 Debt-to-Revenue ratio is 7.64%, and the FY26 Debt-to-Revenue ratio is estimated to be 7.41%.
Debt service above 20% of operating revenues is considered a problem, while 10% is considered
acceptable. Natick remains below these thresholds.
Future debt issuance should be timed to minimize its impact on the operating budget.
Growth in Debt P er Capita
Natick’s debt per capita has grown significantly due to the addition of Natick High School (2011), Kennedy
Middle School (2018), and the Community Senior Center (2011). These debt issuances were well-timed, as
they:
a) received favorable bid prices,
b) were issued at low-interest rates,
c) followed several years of declining debt service amounts, and
d) involved projects funded through debt exclusions.
Massachusetts Debt Limits
Massachusetts General Law Chapter 44, Section 10 states that, except as otherwise provided by law, a city or
town cannot authorize debt exceeding 5% of the community’s equalized valuation (EQV). However, with
approval from the Municipal Finance Oversight Board, debt can exceed this limit up to 10%. Natick’s Aggregate
EQV ratio is 1.1%, well within the allowable limit.

Debt Limit Analysis
Debt Limit: Under Massachusetts General Law (Chapter 44, Section 10), a town’s debt issuance is limited to 5%
of the "equalized valuation" (EQV) of taxable property unless approval to exceed this limit is obtained from the
Municipal Finance Oversight Board.
Natick’s most recent EQV is $12,163,959,770, which sets the Debt Limit at 5% of EQV, or $608,197,988.
Outstanding Debt: Outstanding debt refers to the total amount of the Town’s existing debt obligations. Annual
payments of interest and principal are included in the Town’s Shared Expenses budget, based on the debt
service schedule for each bond issuance.
The chart above illustrates the debt limit and outstanding debt from FY 2021 to FY 2026 projections. In FY
2026, the outstanding debt as a percentage of the debt limit is estimated to be 22%, representing a 3%
decrease from FY 2025. This widening gap indicates an increasing borrowing capacity for the Town of Natick.
Prudent Financial Management: Despite remaining well below the borrowing cap, the Town maintains prudent
financial management by actively monitoring the General Fund’s leverage ratios to ensure its ability to repay
debt. In the interest of long-term fiscal health and sustainability, the Town Administration collaborates closely
with department heads. This collaboration emphasizes the use of alternative funding sources and prioritizes
capital spending, underscoring the Town’s commitment to responsible financial practices.
13

--- Page 18 ---

Capital & Debt Ratio Analysis
Debt Service and Credit Ratings: Debt service payments account for 24% of the General Fund Shared Expense
Budget, covering the financing costs and fees associated with capital projects. The debt ratio, which represents
total debt payments as a percentage of revenues, is a key indicator of the town's ability to repay its debt. This
metric is critically evaluated by independent credit agencies during each bond issuance.
In June 2023, the Town maintained its AAA credit rating from S&P Global, and in June 2024, FitchRatings also
reaffirmed Natick’s AAA credit rating.
Debt Ratio Management: Following the Town's Financial Management Principles, efforts are focused on keeping
the debt burden ratio between 8% and 10% to ensure affordability and fiscal stability. The recommended upper
limit remains at 10%, as shown in the left-hand chart.
In recent years, the Town has successfully managed its debt ratio below 10%. The debt ratio rose to 8.9% in
FY 2024 due to two bond issuances in the prior fiscal year, addressing delayed capital projects from the COVID-
19 period. Adjustments in borrowing strategies have since moderated the debt ratio, reducing it to 7.41% in FY
2026. No long-term bonds are scheduled for issuance in FY 2025 to ease pressure on the Debt Services Budget.
Capital Planning T rends: On the other hand, capital project demands have been increasing and have outpaced
capital financing due to a growing number of projects and inflations. The significant rise in FY 2026 and FY
2027 is driven by key projects such as the Memorial School Project and Natick High School construction. These
figures remain subject to change as the Town continues to evaluate alternative funding strategies.
Future Borrowing Plans and Challenges: In FY 2026, the Town plans to issue a long-term bond, anticipating
future interest rate reductions. However, all outstanding capital projects will be carefully assessed before
financing. With significant operating budget challenges in FY 2026, a large portion of Free Cash is being
allocated to operations rather than capital investments, limiting the Town’s ability to fund additional projects.
Outstanding capital appropriations will need to be reevaluated, and rescinded, if necessary, to maintain fiscal
responsibility while addressing critical capital needs.

TOWN MODERATOR 
  
JEFF ALDERSON 
moderator@natickma.org ◆ (508) 810-7530 
13 East Central St. Natick, MA 01760 ◆ www.natickma.gov 
               
 
To Town Meeting Members in Preparation for Fall Annual Town Meeting 2025 
  
Thank you all for helping to make my inaugural Town Meeting this past Spring a success.  I 
deeply appreciate all Town Meeting Members' continued commitment to democracy at 
the local level.  Fall Annual Town Meeting 2025 will commence on Tuesday 10/21/25 at 7:30 
PM at the  Kennedy Middle School Auditorium located at 165 Mill Street.   
 
I want to bring to your attention that the Warrant for this Town Meeting includes two 
Articles that may  impact the future of how Town Meeting is run.  A motion under Article 15 
seeks to establish a Hybrid Town Meeting Committee with a goal of recommending a 
framework for conducting hybrid town meetings.  Motions under Article 32 seek to amend 
Town ByLaws in order to adopt the 4th Edition of Town Meeting Time, and ensure that our 
existing rules for Town Meeting are reconciled with this edition.  Both of these Articles 
may positively impact our ability to hold a more accessible and inclusive meeting. 
 
Please do review the Town Meeting Member Handbook prior to the ﬁrst night of Town 
Meeting, which is available on the Town Meeting webpage (see: 
natickma.gov/375/Town-Meeting-Information). I also encourage you to review the Town 
Meeting New Member Orientation materials, recently updated for FATM 2025 (see: 
natickma.gov/DocumentCenter/View/19549/Town-Meeting-Member-Orientation)  
 
I encourage all Members to sign up for email and/or text alerts related to Town Meeting 
using the Alerts & Notiﬁcations feature of the Town website (see: 
natickma.gov/list.aspx 
and select “Town Meeting”).  The agenda for each night of Town Meeting will be posted to 
the FATM 2025 page (see: natickma.gov/2287/2025-Fall-Annual-Town-Meeting)  and 
an alert will be sent if you subscribe. These are the only notiﬁcations that will be sent 
regarding agendas and supplemental materials in advance of each night of Town Meeting. 
 
I look forward to seeing all of you together again in person on October 21st. 
 
Je昀昀 Alderson, Town Moderator 
 
Natick Town Hall ◆ 13 East Central Street ◆ Natick, Massachusetts 01760 ◆ 508-647-6400 ◆ www.natickma.gov

NATICK PLANNING BOARD REPORT 
2025 FALL ANNUAL TOWN MEETING 
 
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~ 
 
October 3, 2025 
 
Articles requiring a public hearing 
 
The Planning Board held public hearings for the zoning bylaw-related Town Meeting articles, per 
M.G.L. c.40A s. 5 as follows: 
 
Warrant Article Date(s) of Public Hearing 
20 8/13/25; 8/27/25; 9/10/25; 9/25/25 
21 8/13/25; 8/27/25; 9/10/25; 9/25/25 
22 8/13/25; 8/27/25; 9/10/25; 9/25/25 
23 8/13/25; 8/27/25; 9/10/25; 9/25/25; 9/30/25 
24 8/13/25; 8/27/25; 9/10/25; 9/25/25; 9/30/25 
25 8/13/25; 8/27/25; 9/10/25; 9/25/25 
26 8/13/25; 8/27/25; 9/10/25 
29 8/13/25; 8/27/25; 9/10/25; 9/25/25 
   
Article 20 – Amend Zoning Bylaws: §V-F – Removal of Earth Products 
The Planning Board reviewed Article 20 at its meeting of September 25, voting to recommend 
Favorable Action and closing the public hearing. Vote 5-0-0.  
This article, which is sponsored by the Planning Board, addresses a flaw in the wording of the 
1974 bylaw, which has the unintended consequence of prohibiting the temporary removal or 
offsite storage of gravel, earth, or similar materials as part of excavation and construction on a 
site.  
Article 21 – Amend Zoning Bylaws: §V-G Flooding 
The Planning Board reviewed Article 21 at its meeting of September 25, voting to recommend 
Favorable Action and voted to close the public hearing. Vote 5-0-0.  
The Planning Board is the sponsor of this article, which removes §V-G Flooding from the Zoning 
Bylaw. Since the introduction of this section, the Town has adopted §III-A.3, the Floodplain 
District and Stormwater Management Bylaws. These two new bylaws, together with effective 
engineering and construction practices can be used to manage stormwater in Natick, ultimately 
protecting properties during storm events. 
Article 22 - Amend Zoning Bylaws: Section 200 – Definitions and Limited Site Plan Review 
The Planning Board reviewed Article 22 at its meeting of September 25, voting to recommend 
Favorable Action and voting to close the public hearing. Vote 5-0-0.  
This article is sponsored by the Planning Board and continues the Board’s effort to update and 
clarify elements of the Zoning Bylaw in 2024. In her review of the vote taken in the 2024 Spring 
Annual Town Meeting modification of Section VI-DD, the Attorney General directed the Town to 
modify its proposed definition of Limited Site Plan Review to align with the state. 
 
 
 
27

--- Page 32 ---

Planning Board Report to 2025 Fall Annual Town Meeting 
Page 2 of 2 
 
 
Article 23 – Amend Zoning Bylaws: Use Regulation Schedule 
The Planning Board reviewed Article 23 at its meeting of September 30, and the Board voted to 
recommend Favorable Action. Vote 4-0-0. Mr. Nottonson was not present on September 30. 
This article, which is sponsored by the Planning Board, continues the comprehensive review and 
updating of the Use Regulation Schedule in the Zoning Bylaws that has taken place over the past 
several Town Meetings 
 
Article 24 – Amend Zoning Bylaws: Use Regulation Schedule 
The Planning Board reviewed Article 24 at its meetings of September 30, at which the Board 
voted to recommend Favorable Action. Vote 4-0-0. Mr. Nottonson was not present at this 
meeting. 
This article, which is sponsored by the Planning Board, establishes a zoning district with five 
subdistricts in West Natick in the Route 135 corridor and environs, as well as making nominal 
adjustments to the Limited Commercial (LC) district in West Natick and a small part of North 
Main Street. The application of form-based zoning is designed to improve walkability; advance 
non-vehicular mobility; and foster new development that supports the surrounding residential 
neighborhoods north and south of the railroad tracks and the users of the West Natick commuter 
rail station. 
 
Article 25 – Amend Zoning Bylaws: Accessory Dwelling Units 
The Planning Board reviewed Article 25 at its meeting of September 25, at which the Board 
voted to recommend Favorable Action. Vote 5-0-0.  
This article, which is sponsored by the Town Administrator, modifies language originally voted by 
Town Meeting in the fall of 2024 and brings it into line with state requirements. In her review of 
the 2024 vote, the Massachusetts Attorney General requested the modifications and 
clarifications detailed in the motion for Article 25. 
Article 26 – Amend Zoning Map: 0 Worcester Street (Assessor’s Map 23, Lot 69A) 
The Planning Board reviewed Article 26 at its meeting of September 10, at which the Board 
voted to recommend Favorable Action and voted to close the public hearing. Vote 4-0-0. Mr. 
Landry was not present at the September 10 meeting. 
This article, which is sponsored by the Town Administrator, proposes to change the zoning of a 
small parcel that is currently in commercial use from Residential to Commercial II (C-II) zoning. A 
pronounced grade change separates the land that this article proposes to rezone from the 
adjacent adjoining property that is in residential use.
 
Article 29 – Amend Zoning Bylaws: §V-H Signage and Advertising Devices 
The Planning Board reviewed Article 29 at its meeting of September 25, at which the Board 
voted to recommend Favorable Action. Vote 5-0-0. Mr. Nottonson was not present at the 
September 25 meeting. 
This article is a citizen petition sponsored by Natick Center Associates. The Planning Board 
worked collaboratively with the sponsor throughout the development of this article.

Consideration of Use of Consent Agenda at FATM 2025
I suggest the following motion for Town Meeting Member’s consideration regarding use of
Consent Agenda motion:
Move that a CONSENT AGENDA shall be in order during the First Session of this Fall Annual
Town Meeting; provided, however that the Moderator must ensure that said motion is 
published in the Finance Committee Recommendation Book which is required to be provided 
at least seven(7) days prior to the opening of the First Session of this Fall Annual Town 
Meeting. 
The Moderator shall propose to Town Meeting Members a “Consent Agenda” in the form of a 
motion listing all articles and respective motions which (based on the advice of the Finance 
Committee, Town Clerk and Town Counsel) the Moderator deems to be non-controversial. 
At said First Session of the meeting, seven (7) Town Meeting Members may be recognized by
the Moderator so that any article shall be removed from the Consent Agenda and debated 
and voted upon in accordance with the provisions of Town Meeting rules and practices. All 
articles remaining in the Consent Agenda shall then be voted upon by a single 2/3 vote 
without sponsor presentation or debate.

ARTICLE 15 - Establishment of a Hybrid Town Meeting Committee
MOTION:
WHEREAS, the Town of Natick recognizes the importance of maximizing voter 
participation and engagement in its democratic processes;
WHEREAS, the advent of technology offers new opportunities to facilitate broader 
access to Town Meeting proceedings while maintaining the integrity and deliberative 
nature of the meeting;
3
35

--- Page 40 ---

2025 FALL ANNUAL TOWN MEETING
CONSENT AGENDA MOTION
WHEREAS, it is deemed prudent to establish a committee to thoroughly research, 
analyze, and propose a comprehensive plan for the implementation of hybrid town 
meetings in Natick.
Therefore, it is hereby moved that the Town of Natick establish a committee to be 
known as the "Hybrid Town Meeting Committee" with the following charter:
1. Purpose: The Hybrid Town Meeting Committee shall be charged with the 
responsibility of studying and recommending a comprehensive framework for the 
conduct of hybrid town meetings in Natick, including but not limited to:
 Reviewing the hybrid meeting practices currently in place at 
Representative Town Meetings in Massachusetts.
 Evaluating various technological platforms and solutions for remote 
participation.
 Developing protocols and procedures to ensure secure and verifiable 
remote voting.
 Addressing issues related to accessibility and equity for all participants, 
regardless of their technological capabilities.
 Proposing amendments to existing bylaws or the Town Charter as 
necessary to facilitate hybrid meetings.
 Considering the logistical and financial implications of implementing hybrid
meetings.
 Recommending best practices for maintaining the decorum and 
deliberative nature of Town Meeting in a hybrid format.
2. Composition: The Hybrid Town Meeting Committee shall consist of nine (9) 
members, appointed as follows:
 Eight (8) Town Meeting members appointed by the Moderator.
 One (1) member representing Natick Pegasus appointed by the 
Moderator.
3. Reporting: The Hybrid Town Meeting Committee shall submit its 
recommendations to the Select Board and Town Meeting at the 2026 Spring 
Annual Town Meeting. The report shall include a detailed proposal for the 
implementation of hybrid town meetings, including any proposed bylaw 
amendments or other necessary actions.
4. Funding: The Town shall appropriate the sum of $10,000 from FY 2026 State 
Aid to support the work of the Hybrid Town Meeting Committee, including but not 
limited to, the procurement of legal counsel, expert consultations, technological 
assessments, and public outreach efforts.
4
36

--- Page 41 ---

2025 FALL ANNUAL TOWN MEETING
CONSENT AGENDA MOTION
5. Sunset Clause: Unless otherwise extended by a vote of Town Meeting, the 
Hybrid Town Meeting Committee shall cease to exist upon the submission of its 
final report or by June 30, 2026, whichever comes first.

MOTION B
Move that the Town vote to amend Section 1 Rules of Procedure of Article 3 of 
the bylaws by adding the following words to the beginning of the second 
paragraph of said Section 1:
“In addition to any statutory requirements for public hearings in advance of 
consideration of articles by Representative Town Meeting, the public hearing 
held by the Finance Committee on all matters of business within the warrant for 
any town meeting pursuant to Article 23 Section 4 of these bylaws also 
constitutes a required mandatory condition precedent to consideration by 
Representative Town Meeting. When the requirement of a mandatory condition 
precedent has not met, the Moderator should rule that the motion is not properly
before the meeting and that no vote should be taken except as otherwise 
provided in this Section 1. When mandatory conditions precedent have not 
been met, allowable motions are postponement to a time certain or no action.” 
and by inserting the words 
“In addition,” before the words “The Representative Town Meeting” in the last 
sentence of the current text of said second paragraph and changing the “T” in 
the word “The” of said sentence to lower case so that the second paragraph of 
Section 1 now reads:
“In addition to any statutory requirements for public hearings in advance of 
consideration of articles by Representative Town Meeting, the public hearing 
held by the Finance Committee on all matters of business within the warrant for 
any town meeting pursuant to Article 23 Section 4 of these bylaws also 
constitutes a required mandatory condition precedent to consideration by 
Representative Town Meeting. When the requirement of a mandatory condition 
precedent has not met, the Moderator should rule that the motion is not properly
before the meeting and that no vote should be taken except as otherwise 
provided in this Section 1. When mandatory conditions precedent have not 
been met, allowable motions under these bylaws are ‘postponement to a time 
certain’ or ‘no action’. In addition, the Representative Town Meeting may, by a 
2/3 rds vote, waive any requirement in the bylaws for a public hearing, unless 
required by statute or the Town Charter, on specified or particular matters of 
business included within the articles of any Town Meeting.

FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION
Mr. Townsend presented this article.  He shared that the appropriation will be sourced from 
State Aid in an amount just under $60,000.  He shared that we budget our State Aid number 
based on the Governor’s initial estimates.  However, State Aid exceeded the initial estimate 
by over $200,000, and is the funding source for this Article.
He noted that there is a bill for the golf course in this Article, which we don’t usually do for 
Enterprise funds. The Administration decided to fund that invoice through this Article, and 
make an adjustment in the Indirects calculations.
Motions & Debate
Members asked various questions regarding the specific unpaid invoices and funding: 
Does the town have a credit account with Amazon business?  Mr. Townsend said yes, they 
do take our purchase orders - and confirmed that these are unpaid invoices.
46

--- Page 51 ---

A member noted that there are identical amounts for the same vendor - are they actually two 
different invoices?  Mr. Townsend said yes, they did confirm that, it’s just a recurring charge 
that is the same each month.
A member asked whether the date of the Sentinel invoice is the date of the service provided 
or the bill date.  Mr. Townsend said it was the bill date.
A member asked about one of the bills for software (“Brightly) and whether that was an 
annual bill or a one time expense? Bill Spratt, Executive Director of the Department of Public 
Works and Facilities, explained that this was a one time fee for consulting and project 
management for implementing the software.  That was a year-long project.  The issue with 
this bill was that the software itself is approximately $66,000/year, but they had already paid 
that.  So, there was some confusion about what this bill was for which led to a delay, which is 
why it has ended up on this list out of the fiscal year. The software itself is typically paid out of
our IT budget but the project management expense would have come out of DPW.
A member asked where the rest of the FY2026 State Aid would be going.  Mr. Townsend said
it was being reserved for Spring but Mr. Errickson added that it could be used for other things 
this session as it comes up.
NOTE: See Recommendation Book Appendix for invoice detail.
The committee voted 13-0-0 to recommend Favorable Action on the subject matter of 
Article 4.

FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION 
This motion was presented by Town Administrator Jamie Erickson. He explained that total 
new growth is currently expected to be $2,050,000 and this appropriation approximately 
represents the difference between budgeted new growth ($1,100,000) and expected actual 
new growth. As of the printing deadline for the Finance Committee recommendations book, 
FY26 new growth had not yet been certified. If FY26 New Growth is not certified prior to the 
Town Meeting session at which this Article is considered, or if such New Growth is certified at
an amount insufficient to meet the proposed appropriation, Town Meeting should expect an 
amended motion.
In response to Finance Committee member questions, Mr. Erickson stated that (i) the 
proposed appropriations of FY26 new growth had been reviewed by the Assessor’s office and
(ii) the proposed Operation Stabilization Fund would bring the balance in such fund up to the 
level of the Town’s target.
The committee voted 13-0-0 to recommend Favorable Action on the subject matter of 
Article 5.

Article 6
PEG Access and Cable Related Fund
(Town Administrator )
ARTICLE LANGUAGE
To see what sum of money the Town will vote to appropriate from the PEG Access and Cable

by Chapter 44, Section 53F ¾ of the General Laws, as amended, to fund PEG access
programming, as well as certain other municipal cable related expenses; or otherwise act
thereon.
PURPOSE OF THE ARTICLE
To appropriate from the PEG Access and Cable Related Fund, established under Article 1 of the 2019
Special Town Meeting #1 as authorized by Chapter 44, Section 53F ¾ of the General Laws, as 
amended, to fund PEG access programming, as well as certain other municipal cable related 
expenses; or otherwise act thereon.
FINANCE COMMITTEE RECOMMENDATION
The Finance Committee
took the following action:
RECOMMENDATION: Favorable
QUANTUM OF VOTE: 13-0-0
DATE VOTED: 9/25/2025
MOTION (Requires a Majority Vote)
Move that the Town vote to appropriate from the PEG Access and Cable Related Fund, established by
vote of the 2019 Special Town Meeting #1, Article 1, as authorized by Chapter 44, Section 53F 3⁄4 of 
the General Laws, as amended, the sum of $310,059.98 to fund PEG access programming.
FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION
Town Administration explained that this is the semi-annual appropriation request to transfer 
funds remitted to the town, by the three cable companies licensed to operate in Natick. These
are the fees collected from the end-consumers, held in a segregated account until 
appropriated, and transferred to Natick Pegasus. 
Reminder: The traditional cable subscription business model is “evolving”. Consumers are 
cord-cutting, and moving away from paying cable subscriptions - including the fees that 
currently fund Natick Pegasus. In light of this long term trend, the town needs to consider and 
plan for a different funding source for Natick Pegasus. 
The committee voted 13-0-0 to recommend Favorable Action on the subject matter of 
Article 6.
~~ END OF ARTICLE ~~

FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION 
Mr. Townsend presented this article. He explained that the request here was to appropriate a 
little over $189,000 from Select Board expenses, which is a line item in the budget for these 
kinds of collective bargaining agreements. These CBAs are for the police unions for both 
Patrol Officers and Superior Officers.
Mr. Errickson further added that there is a significant change to the Patrol Officer page table 
to update it a bit to make it more modern. Some other standard things were adjusted such as 
COLAs and a few other small language adjustments.
Motions & Debate
A member noted he was uncomfortable that the MOU said that it was “off the record.” Mr. 
Errickson said that really the “off the record” is about the Select Board, not Town Meeting. 
A member asked which line item this falls under in the budget in terms of where it goes on the
police budget. Mr. Townsend said it is multiple lines of that budget. This would be going 
towards the salary lines for the police department (though there are separate ones for 
different types of officers). However, Town Meeting only votes it as a bottom line number.
The committee voted 13-0-0 to recommend Favorable Action on the subject matter of 
Article 7.

FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION 
Jon Marshall, Deputy Town Administrator for Operations, presented the capital plan.  Mr. 
Marshall explained that the capital request is lighter than might be expected for a number of 
reasons, but the primary one is that the town is engaged in a comprehensive financial 
56

--- Page 61 ---

planning process to evaluate how they will fund capital projects going forward, particularly 
those that are funded through borrowing (to ensure we have the recurring funds to pay for 
borrowing costs).  That analysis will be integrated into the development of the five year capital
improvement plan in the spring. In the meantime, the town is focused on only those projects 
that are the most urgent.
Other key notes from the Finance Committee and Capital Subcommittee hearings:
There is no request for additional money for the roadway improvement plan because 
they are able to fully fund all the projects they intend to do this season through existing 
state money (chapter 90).
We are still comfortably within the borrowing capacity recommended by the 
Massachusetts Department of Revenue.  However, the hesitancy to borrow more at 
this time is more about managing our debt service budget.
Inflation continues to be an issue, especially on certain items.  For example, the town 
looked back at its 2021-2026 capital improvement plan and noted that there was a 
59% difference between the projected costs of the kinds of vehicles we need to 
purchase now and their quoted cost.
The committee voted 13-0-0 to recommend Favorable Action on the subject matter of 
Article 9, with respect to both Motion A and Motion B.

Article 10
Appropriation for Memorial Elementary School Feasibility Study
(School Committee)
ARTICLE LANGUAGE
To see if the Town will vote to appropriate, borrow or transfer from available funds, an amount
of money to be expended under the direction of the School Building Committee for the 
Memorial Elementary School building project, currently located at 107 Eliot Street, Natick, 
Massachusetts, for which feasibility study the Town may be eligible for a grant from the 
Massachusetts School Building Authority. The MSBA’s grant program is a non-entitlement, 
discretionary program based on need, as determined by the MSBA, and any costs the Town 
incurs in connection with the feasibility study in excess of any grant approved by and received
from the MSBA shall be the sole responsibility of the Town; or otherwise act thereon.
PURPOSE OF THE ARTICLE
To appropriate, borrow or transfer from available funds, an amount of money to be expended 
under the direction of the School Building Committee for the Memorial Elementary School 
building project, currently located at 107 Eliot Street, Natick, Massachusetts, for which 
feasibility study the Town may be eligible for a grant from the Massachusetts School Building 
Authority. The MSBA’s grant program is a non-entitlement, discretionary program based on 
need, as determined by the MSBA, and any costs the Town incurs in connection with the 
feasibility study in excess of any grant approved by and received from the MSBA shall be the 
sole responsibility of the Town; or otherwise act thereon.
FINANCE COMMITTEE RECOMMENDATION
The Finance Committee
took the following action:
RECOMMENDATION: Favorable
QUANTUM OF VOTE: 13-0-0
DATE VOTED: 9/30/2025
MOTION (Requires a 2/3rds Vote)
Move that the Town of Natick appropriate the amount of Two Million Six Hundred Thousand 
($2,600,000) Dollars for the purpose of paying costs to conduct a feasibility study for the 
Memorial Elementary School building project, currently located at 107 Eliot Street, Natick, 
Massachusetts, including the payment of all costs incidental or related thereto, and for which 
the Town of Natick may be eligible for a grant from the Massachusetts School Building 
Authority ("MSBA"), said amount to be expended under the direction of the School Building 
Committee. To meet this appropriation the Select Board is authorized to borrow said amount
65

--- Page 70 ---

under and pursuant to M.G.L. Chapter 44, or pursuant to any other enabling authority. The 
Town of Natick acknowledges that the MSBA's grant program is a non-entitlement, 
discretionary program based on need, as determined by the MSBA, and any costs the Town 
of Natick incurs in excess of any grant approved by and received from the MSBA shall be the 
sole responsibility of the Town of Natick, and that the amount of borrowing authorized 
pursuant to this vote shall be reduced by any grant amount set forth in the Feasibility Study
Agreement that may be executed between the Town of Natick and the MSBA.
FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION 
 
Dr. Melissa Spash, Superintendent of Natick Public Schools, presented this article along with Elise 
Gorseth, Chair of the School Committee, Karen Ghilani, Principal from Memorial School, Matt Gillis, 
Deputy Superintendent for Finance, Stephen Meyler, Chair of Memorial School Building Committee, 
and Jamie Errickson, Town Administrator.
The purpose of this article is to fund a feasibility study and schematic design for a future Memorial 
Elementary School building project. The request for $2,600,000 would be funded through new 
borrowing after discussion of funding options with the Town Administration.
Natick Public Schools were invited into the eligibility process with the MSBA in December 2024, and a 
feasibility study is the next step in the process. Approval of Article 10 would provide funding for 
modules 3 and 4, and allow the Town to complete a feasibility study and schematic design (see MSBA
Process & Approvals as well as MSBA Building Process Overview). The funding would allow the 
Memorial School Building Committee to define a preferred solution, develop reliable cost estimates, 
and bring a full project proposal to the community.
Dr. Spash also explained that Natick’s window to secure this funding and stay on track with the MSBA 
application deadline is about to close on October 31 (270 days after being invited to Module 1).  Natick
is seeking an extension, but it is not likely to be a very long one. Favorable Action by Fall Annual Town
Meeting 2025 is essential to keeping on track for the MSBA process. The current projected timeline 
includes a debt exclusion vote in 2027 - 2028 before construction could begin.
MSBA Process & Approvals
66

--- Page 71 ---

MSBA Building Process Overview
The MSBA invited Natick into the eligibility phase based on four criteria:
● Elimination of existing severe overcrowding
● Prevention of severe overcrowding expected to result from increased enrollment.
● Replacement, renovation, or modernization of school facility systems, such as roofs, windows, 
boilers, heating and ventilation systems, to increase energy conservation and decrease energy
related costs in a school facility
● Replacement of or addition to obsolete buildings in order to provide for a full range of programs
consistent with state and approved local requirements.
67

--- Page 72 ---

Supporting examples for each criteria were included in the April 2024 Statement of Interest, which was
the basis of MSBA’s invitation to the eligibility phase.
Overcrowding and Inadequate Space for Programs: The school was built for 312 - 348 students 
but currently serves 440 - 450 students. Hallways and closets are being used as instructional spaces, 
Pre-K has had to be moved off-site, and Memorial cannot support a full special education / english 
language learner program. There is inadequate storage for afterschool programs, and core spaces for 
Art, Music, Dining, Gym, and Library are undersized for the current population.
Aging and Failing Building Systems: Electrical system is old and undersized, windows, doors, and 
masonry are deteriorating with leaking and other issues. The building is not ADA compliant, and the 
front office has no view of the school, which can be a safety issue.
Loss of Core Educational & Community Functions: Playground equipment near end of life, current
building cannot support preschool, full special education and multilingual learner programs, flexible 
spaces and cafetorium are being used as classrooms and small group spaces.
Dr. Spash outlined how the proposed project aims to create a modern elementary school for 600 
learners, a neighborhood preschool, a full special education program, and space for multilingual 
learners, and adequate core spaces. The MSBA sets the final enrollment and reimbursement rate and 
Natick will receive the enrollment from MSBA in the next phase.Based on their current estimates, the 
reimbursement rate for this project would be 45%.
Mr. Gillis outlined the sub-costs of the feasibility and schematic design funding.  The funding would 
cover hiring an Owners Project Manager, architectural plans, geothermal test wells, and consulting 
(and also a little contingency buffer). The $2,600,000 figure is based on other communities as a 
reference point for coming up with these amounts.
Regarding funding sources, Jamie Errickson, Town Administrator, explained that free cash would not 
work with the October 31 funding deadline, which is likely before the Town will have certified free 
cash. Additionally, the Town generally spends free cash on more immediate projects. While the Town 
does have $4.9 million of unspent funds borrowed for the Kennedy Middle School project, these can 
only be reappropriated for projects of a similar useful life. Since the Kennedy Middle School borrowing 
was for a useful life of 20 years, it cannot be used for a feasibility study, which has a useful life of 5 
years. New growth would not be sufficient to cover the requested appropriation for Article 10.
Therefore, new borrowing is the preferred method of funding Article 10. The authorization would not 
necessarily be borrowed right away, so the Town would do short term borrowing, only making interest 
payments over a couple of years, allowing us to keep our interest costs down until we can wrap the 
2.6 million into the larger, longer-term borrowing for the construction project after design work is done.
Questions from the Committee
A member asked how many Johnson Elementary students were added to the Memorial School 
population, and Dr. Spash confirmed that 60 students went to Memorial after the Johnson school 
closure.
A member asked if the other elementary schools were at or over capacity. Dr. Spash answered that 
most were at capacity, though several schools have modular classrooms which are being used 
beyond their recommended useful life and this was of interest to the MSBA when considering Natick’s 
Statement of Interest. There are also 5 preschool classrooms at the East School because they cannot 
fit in the existing elementary school spaces. Every elementary school has had to get creative with 
providing small group or interventionist spaces in hallways, offices, and shared spaces.
68

--- Page 73 ---

Dr. Spash confirmed that while the building is over capacity, it is important to stress that the building is
obsolete. It was built in 1966 and is now seriously deteriorating.  To the extent there is overcrowding, a
lot of it is at the pre-school level.  But, more fundamentally, even though enrollment isn’t growing, the 
nature of our student population is changing in ways that impact physical space; for example, more 
special needs children and English language learners means that we need more space for small 
group instruction.
A member asked about possible increases on the reimbursement rate, but these are all based on 
different design options, and is a more appropriate question for the Memorial School Building 
Committee during the feasibility study and design process. Increased reimbursement rates have 
historically been based on energy efficient designs, renewable energy sources, and past maintenance 
history.
The Finance Committee members expressed support for the Article and gratitude to the presentation 
team, and had little debate. Some members expressed concerns about design outcomes or financial 
implications of varying reimbursement rates, which are relevant to future stages of the project. Finance
Committee, Town Meeting, and the Natick community will hear more details about this project as it 
progresses.
The committee voted 13-0-0 to recommend Favorable Action on the subject matter of 
Article 10.
~~ END OF ARTICLE ~~

FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION 
This motion was presented by Select Board member Richard Sidney. Mr. Sidney explained 
that the Select Board believes that the current table of Select Board appointments is outdated
and includes some boards and/or committees that are no longer needed and which the Select
Board is not otherwise required (by state law, Town Charter, Town Bylaws or intermunicipal 
agreement) to make. The motion is not intended to limit the scope of the Select Board’s 
appointments, but to list only those appointments about which the Select Board has no 
discretion. The Select Board could then continue to make (or cease to make) discretionary 
appointments without coming to Town Meeting to amend the table.
A Finance Committee member noted that the motion omitted a committee that is required by 
72

--- Page 77 ---

state law. In response to a Finance Committee member, Mr. Sidney stated that the table and 
motion had not been reviewed by Town Counsel. The Finance Committee voted to continue 
the hearing to a later date to allow for corrections to be made. 
At the continued hearing, a revised motion was presented.  A Finance Committee member 
asked if any of the committees being removed from the current table were created by Town 
Meeting. Mr. Sidney stated that he was not certain. Another Finance Committee member 
noted that several of the citations to Massachusetts General Law in the revised motion were 
incorrect. A Finance Committee member expressed concern that the table of appointments 
only includes as ‘required’ those appointments established under state law, Town Charter, 
Town Bylaw and intermunicipal agreement, but does not include those appointments (if any) 
established by direct vote of Town Meeting. Several Finance Committee members considered
the aim of the motion to have merit, but that the revised motion still had errors and appeared 
not to have had sufficient review.

Article 12
Amend or Repeal By law Article 27, Information Systems Advisory Board
(Select Board)
ARTICLE LANGUAGE
To see if the Town will vote to amend or repeal Bylaw Article 27, Information Systems 
Advisory Board; or otherwise act thereon.
PURPOSE OF THE ARTICLE
To amend or repeal Bylaw Article 27, Information Systems Advisory Board; or otherwise act 
thereon.
FINANCE COMMITTEE RECOMMENDATION
The Finance Committee
took the following action:
RECOMMENDATION: Refer to Sponsor
QUANTUM OF VOTE: 10-2-0
DATE VOTED: 9/11/2025
MOTION (Requires a Majority Vote)
 Move that the Town vote to repeal bylaw Article 27, Information Systems Advisory Board.
FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION 
Richard Sidney, Select Board member, presented this article. He explained that this is part of 
a review of all the boards and committees that the Select Board appoints. As part of that 
effort, they realized that the Cable Advisory Board (CAB) and the Information Systems 
Advisory Board (ISAB) have been co-appointed for at least the last 8 years. The Select Board
wants to adjust the charge and description of a combined board.  Because the Information 
Systems Advisory Board is in by-law, re-writing that charge is difficult and requires Town 
Meeting action to ratify. The Select Board wants to keep a combined board in existence, but 
they want to take it out of the by-law. 
Multiple Finance Committee members expressed various levels of concern about this 
proposal. Most of the concerns centered on the fact that boards and committees not 
specifically required in the bylaws can be sunset by the appointing authority without additional
process or Town Meeting input. Multiple members expressed concern that the importance 
and complexity of information systems and technology is only increasing, and that a group of 
professionals volunteering their time and advice is of value. One Fincom member stressed 
the importance of having more input on critical functions, like security, not less. 
Members discussed the logic of having (most) members of the ISAB overlap with the CAB. 
76

--- Page 81 ---

The main function of the Cable Advisory Board is to negotiate the contract terms of the three 
cable licenses operating in town - and then advise the Select Board as license granting 
authority. This is an infrequent task - which does have some limited technology and 
networking components. 
Motions and Debate:
Motions were made and seconded to: 1- recommend Favorable Action, and 2 - Refer the 
article back to the Sponsor. 
Supporters of Favorable Action argued that there wasn’t a downside to removing the ISAB 
from the bylaws, and that it makes the process of modifying the charge and composition of 
the Board much simpler. Another proponent argued that if it’s not required by statute, it should
not be in the bylaws. 
Supporters of Referral argued that Information Systems are critical and complex, and that 
weakening the requirement for having an advisory board is ill advised. 
The motion for referral passed by a vote of 10-2-0.
For reference:
Current Bylaw Article 27 – TO BE REPEALED:
ARTICLE 27
INFORMATION SYSTEMS ADVISORY BOARD
Section 1 Powers and Duties 
There shall be an Information Systems Advisory Board which shall advise the Town on policies, 
procedures, priorities, and planning of the information systems of the Town. 
Section 2 Composition, Term of Office 
Said Board shall be composed of seven (7) members who shall be appointed by the Select Board 
from within the Town and shall not be full-time employees of the Town. When available, a minimum of 
four (4) of said seven (7) members appointed by the Select Board shall possess knowledge and 
experience in the field of information systems and services. Appointees to the Information Systems 
Advisory Board shall serve for three (3) year terms commencing July first. In the event of a vacancy 
occurring in the membership other than by the expiration of the term of a member, the Select Board 
shall within sixty (60) days after a vacancy occurs appoint a successor to serve for the balance of the 
unexpired term. 
Section 3 Meetings 
Meetings of said Board are to be held at least four (4) times each calendar year.
The committee voted 10-2-0 to recommend Referral to Sponsor on the subject matter 
of Article 12.

(Select Board)

took the following action:

MOTION (Requires a Majority Vote)
Move that the Town accept the provisions of Massachusetts General Laws Chapter 41

FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION 
Text of M.G.L. Chapter 41 Section 110A
Section 110A: Office hours on Saturday 
Section 110A. Any public office in any city or town may remain closed on any or all Saturdays 
as may be determined from time to time, in a city by the city council, subject to the provisions 
of the city charter, or, in a town, by vote of the town at a special or regular town meeting, and 
the provisions of section nine of chapter four shall apply in the case of such closing of any 
such office on any Saturday to the same extent as if such Saturday were a legal holiday. 
Discussion and Questions:
Andrew Ghobrial, Town Clerk, presented the article. He explained that this law, if adopted by 
the town, would allow the Clerk’s Office to close on Saturdays as we see fit.  It would not 
impact the ability to hold a public hearing or a meeting on Saturday if it so chose.  Once it is 
accepted, it would allow the Clerk's Office to close on certain Saturdays before Town 
78

--- Page 83 ---

Elections. He noted three elections since he started - and during those three Saturdays, they 
saw hardly any traffic in the Clerk’s office.  Nobody came in before the spring town election 
despite it being a high profile election due to the override.  As he sees it, this is a waste of 
resources.  He estimates the town spent at least $1,500 for that day. The current law in effect 
dates back to when residents would have to go to town hall to register to vote, but you can 
register in so many different ways now, such as online. 
A member asked to clarify whether this was about the weekend before the election or the last 
weekend before the deadline to register.  Mr. Ghobrial answered that it was the latter. The 
member further asked whether this would allow us to keep the Clerk’s office open on 
Saturdays if we chose to do so.  Mr. Ghobrial said that we would continue to have that option,
this just means we don’t have to do that.
Several members questioned the wording of the M.G.L. Section being adopted, and whether 
it was actually limited solely to the Clerk’s office. Mr. Errickson explained that he had an 
extensive conversation with Town Counsel, who has said this is the proper way to adopt this 
provision, including the flexibility to close the Clerk’s office on those days without other action 
or impact on other town offices or functions. 
Members asked how this change, and the office’s closure would be communicated to the 
community in advance. Mr. Ghobrial indicated that it would become part of the published 
“Political Calendar" published on the website. Members encouraged additional forms of notice
which might better serve the users.  
Motions & Debate:
Motion made and seconded to recommend Favorable Action. Multiple members felt that the 
underlying section of M.G.L. being adopted is badly written, and is unclear - with one arguing 
that adopting it is “collaborating with the Commonwealth in terribly written law.” Another 
member felt that adoption appears to make the town less available to the public.
The Motion to recommend Favorable Action passed 8-0-4.  
 
The committee voted 8-0-4 to recommend Favorable Action on the subject matter of 
Article 13.
~~ END OF ARTICLE ~~

--- Page 84 ---

16:15 Dog License and Kennel License Fees

and all kennels under this section shall be adopted by the Select Board subsequent to a 
Public Hearing. 
FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION 
This motion was presented by Town Clerk, Andrew Ghobrial. Mr Ghobrial explained that this 
motion would remove the dog license and kennel fees from the Town Bylaws so that the 
Select Board would be able to adjust such fees from time to time without Town Meeting 
needing to change to the Bylaws, but that no changes to the fees were being sought at this 
time.
Finance Committee members asked about the required process to change the fees if this 
motion were to pass. Mr. Ghobrial stated that no hearing would be required, but if the Select 
Board were to consider changes to the fees, it would do so only in a public meeting, as 
required by the Open Meeting law.
80

--- Page 85 ---

In response to a Finance Committee member, Mr. Ghobrial stated that the fees for unlicensed
kennels were intentionally omitted from the scope of this motion as those fees are enforced 
by the police through the Animal Control Officer.
Several Finance Committee members indicated their view that this would be helpful in 
streamlining the current onerous process to revise such fees, but expressed some concern 
that a streamlined process would carry some risk that less awareness of proposed changes 
would result. 
The committee voted 12-0-0 to recommend Favorable Action on the subject matter of 
Article 14.

Article 15
Establishment of a Hybrid Town Meeting Committee
(Town Moderator and Select Board )
ARTICLE LANGUAGE
To see what action(s) the Town will take to establish a Hybrid Town Meeting Committee, in
accordance with Section 2-11 (e) of the Town of Natick Home Rule Charter, to study and
recommend a framework for conducting hybrid town meetings, to determine how the
committee shall be constituted, to see what sum of money the Town will vote to raise and
appropriate, transfer from available funds, or otherwise provide for the operation of the
committee; or otherwise act thereon.
PURPOSE OF THE ARTICLE
To establish a Hybrid Town Meeting Committee, in accordance with Section 2-11 (e) of the 
Town of Natick Home Rule Charter, to study and recommend a framework for conducting 
hybrid town meetings, to determine how the committee shall be constituted, to see what sum 
of money the Town will vote to raise and appropriate, transfer from available funds, or 
otherwise provide for the operation of the committee; or otherwise act thereon.
FINANCE COMMITTEE RECOMMENDATION
The Finance Committee
took the following action:
RECOMMENDATION: Favorable
QUANTUM OF VOTE: 13-0-0
DATE VOTED: 9/30/2025
MOTION (Requires a Majority Vote)
Move:
WHEREAS, the Town of Natick recognizes the importance of maximizing voter participation 
and engagement in its democratic processes;
WHEREAS, the advent of technology offers new opportunities to facilitate broader access to 
Town Meeting proceedings while maintaining the integrity and deliberative nature of the 
meeting;
WHEREAS, it is deemed prudent to establish a committee to thoroughly research, analyze, 
and propose a comprehensive plan for the implementation of hybrid town meetings in Natick.
82

--- Page 87 ---

Therefore, it is hereby moved that the Town of Natick establish a committee to be known as 
the "Hybrid Town Meeting Committee" with the following charter:
1. Purpose: The Hybrid Town Meeting Committee shall be charged with the responsibility
of studying and recommending a comprehensive framework for the conduct of hybrid 
town meetings in Natick, including but not limited to:
 Reviewing the hybrid meeting practices currently in place at Representative 
Town Meetings in Massachusetts.
 Evaluating various technological platforms and solutions for remote participation.
 Developing protocols and procedures to ensure secure and verifiable remote 
voting.
 Addressing issues related to accessibility and equity for all participants, 
regardless of their technological capabilities.
 Proposing amendments to existing bylaws or the Town Charter as necessary to 
facilitate hybrid meetings.
 Considering the logistical and financial implications of implementing hybrid 
meetings.
 Recommending best practices for maintaining the decorum and deliberative 
nature of Town Meeting in a hybrid format.
2. Composition: The Hybrid Town Meeting Committee shall consist of nine (9) members,
appointed as follows:
Eight (8) Town Meeting members appointed by the Moderator.
One (1) member representing Natick Pegasus appointed by the Moderator. 
3. Reporting: The Hybrid Town Meeting Committee shall submit its recommendations to 
the Select Board and Town Meeting at the 2026 Spring Annual Town Meeting. The 
report shall include a detailed proposal for the implementation of hybrid town meetings,
including any proposed bylaw amendments or other necessary actions.
83

--- Page 88 ---

4. Funding: The Town shall appropriate the sum of $10,000 from FY 2026 State Aid to 
support the work of the Hybrid Town Meeting Committee, including but not limited to, 
the procurement of legal counsel, expert consultations, technological assessments, 
and public outreach efforts.
Sunset Clause: Unless otherwise extended by a vote of Town Meeting, the Hybrid Town 
Meeting Committee shall cease to exist upon the submission of its final report or by June 30, 
2026, whichever comes first.
FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION
 
The Town Moderator appeared at the hearing for this article.  The Moderator surveyed Town 
Meeting members following the 2025 Spring Annual Town Meeting.  28% of respondents 
indicated that they would attend remotely or consider remote attendance.  Medical issues 
were cited by many of those as a motivating reason.  
Finance Committee members inquired about the timeline and about the composition of the 
study committee.  
The Moderator stated that the absolute earliest that a hybrid town meeting could occur if there
is a positive recommendation is 2026 Fall Annual Town Meeting, but that later was possible 
and may be likely.
Some Finance Committee members were concerned that outreach be conducted to include 
people who do not participate in Town Meeting or people who may be skeptical about a 
hybrid Town Meeting.  The Moderator had already considered the challenge of reaching out 
to people who are not among the highly active participants in town government and who may 
be reluctant or otherwise uninclined to seek appointment.  The Moderator intends to seek a 
variety of perspectives.
Other questions were about other towns that conduct hybrid meetings.  The Moderator 
indicated that several towns conduct hybrid meetings, both representative and universal.  He 
said that Plymouth may be the most notable.  There are a few vendors whose systems 
support operation of a hybrid town meeting, including the vendor that Natick currently uses to 
operate its electronic voting system.
The committee voted 13-0-0 to recommend Favorable Action on the subject matter of 
Article 15.
~~ END OF ARTICLE ~~
84

--- Page 89 ---

85

--- Page 90 ---

domain or otherwise, easements in any land necessary for laying out and acceptance of 
JENNIFER CIRCLE, and any appurtenant drainage, utility or other easements related to 
said JENNIFER CIRCLE and/or to accept grants thereof; and further to authorize the Select 
Board and other Applicable Town of Natick Boards and personnel to take all related actions 
necessary or appropriate to accomplish the purposes of this article; Meaning and intending 
to accept JENNIFER CIRCLE, such that the entirety of this named road is accepted by the 
Town as a public way.
 FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION 
Mr. Errickson, Town Administrator, presented this article. He explained that this is a roadway that is 
seeking to be accepted as a public way.  This is a small subdivision that was constructed in the 90s, 
but it was never accepted at that time as a public way. The Select Board adopted standards for 
accepting roadways. The residents on Jennifer Circle went through the standard process and the road
scored very well on that process. The Select Board has endorsed the advancement of Jennifer Circle 
through the program.
Motions & Debate
A member asked why the roads presented this Town Meeting for acceptance are not public roads 
already. Mr. Errickson said it was different for each Article.  Usually what happens is a developer 
builds a subdivision but then needs to submit the roadway to the town for acceptance but that doesn’t 
always happen.  It isn’t clear why that happened with Jennifer Circle. 
A member asked if the people on unaccepted roads have snow plowing and other town services.  Mr. 
Errickson said yes, that they are plowed for public safety purposes, though there are a few exceptions 
to that.
A member asked if the residents of Jennifer Circle had already requested that work be done on the 
road. Mr. Errickson said that was correct. Another member asked what roadwork needs to be done. 
Mr. Errickson said it isn’t specific but putting the road into the roadway maintenance program so that it 
can be assessed and maintained as part of that program, including proper crack sealing up to 
repaving.
A member asked whether the town has a bond associated with work required of this or other 
subdivisions.  Mr. Errickson said he did not know. Continuing, the member asked whether, by 
accepting this, the town would lose the surety the town has or can the town claim that? Mr. Errickson 
said based on the record, they didn’t find a record of a surety or bond associated with this.
A member asked how many houses were on this street. There are 5-10 houses in it.  
The committee voted 11-0-1 to recommend Favorable Action on the subject matter of 
Article 16.

received through user fees and donations to fund costs associated with land disturbance and

General Laws Chapter 44, section 53E1/2; or otherwise act thereon.
PURPOSE OF THE ARTICLE
To amend Article 41A of the General Bylaws of the Town by adding a new section to establish
and authorize the following revolving fund to utilize monies received through user fees and 
donations to fund costs associated with land disturbance and stormwater management 
programs and services, as provided for under Massachusetts General Laws Chapter 44, 
section 53E1/2; or otherwise act thereon.

The Finance Committee
took the following action:
RECOMMENDATION: Favorable
QUANTUM OF VOTE: 13-0-0
DATE VOTED: 9/16/2025
MOTION (Requires a Majority Vote)
Move that the Town vote, pursuant to Chapter 44, Section 53E1/2 of the Massachusetts 
General Laws, to establish a Stormwater Management Revolving Fund, in order to utilize 
monies received through filing fees associated with Art 79A Stormwater Management and 
Erosion Control Bylaw; by amending article 41A of the Natick Town Bylaws to include a new 
section 18 – entitled “Stormwater Fund.”
FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION 
Claire Rundelli, Conservation Agent, presented this article. This would create a revolving fund
for funds that are received for related to stormwater management. The Stormwater 
Management bylaw was created in 2012, and funds have been collected according to its 
provisions. These funds can’t be utilized until an authorized revolving fund is established. This
action will be followed up by a subsequent authorization to put money in the fund in the 
spring.
90

--- Page 95 ---

A member sought clarification on the source of the funds already collected, as well as funds 
going forward. The Sponsor explained that the funds come from applications for activity 
permitted under the Stormwater Management bylaw. To date, approximately $170,000 has 
been collected - most within the last 1.5 years. These collected funds will be transferred to the
newly established revolving fund next spring. A member asked, and the Sponsor confirmed 
that these will not be classified as restricted funds, and that opinion has been reviewed by 
Town Counsel. 
The committee voted unanimously (13-0-0) to approve the motion to Recommend Favorable 
Action.

The Finance Committee
took the following action:
RECOMMENDATION: Favorable
QUANTUM OF VOTE: 8-5-0
DATE VOTED: 9/30/2025
MOTION (Requires a 2/3rds Vote)
Move that the Town vote to amend Section V-F Removal of Earth Products of the Natick Zoning 
Bylaws by
5. deleting the words “Building Inspector” after the words “… except that the removal of said 
material may be permitted subject to the issuance of a building permit by the …” and before the
words “and only to the extent of excavating for the building foundation…” and replacing with 
the words “Building Commissioner”;
6. deleting the second paragraph which reads “Pre-existing use of premises for the excavation or 
removal of sand and gravel can be continued and extended throughout the premises. Opening 
of new sand or gravel pits may be authorized by the Board of Appeals by special permit 
provided such excavations are not harmful or detrimental to the neighborhood. The Board of 
Appeals may impose time limitations and may require bonds and a continuation of such special
permit may be conditioned upon compliance with the regulations to be made and amended 
from time to time.” in its entirety; and further
7. deleting the first sentence of the third paragraph that reads “In no case shall said material be 
removed from the Town.”
to read as follows
“In any district except an authorized sand or gravel pit the removal from the property of soil, loam, sod,
peat, sand or gravel is prohibited, except that the removal of said material may be permitted subject to
the issuance of a building permit by the Building Commissioner and only to the extent of excavating for
92

--- Page 97 ---

a building foundation, structure, roadway, driveway, walk, or parking area and only if at least an eight-
inch layer of packed loam or the total loam and topsoil excavated in the project, whichever is less, is 
left covering all regraded area of the lot.
Removal of topsoil other than specifically permitted in this by-law is classified as stripping and is 
prohibited. (Art. 51 A.T.M. 1974)” .
FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION
Ms. Loomis, Director of Community and Economic Development noted that the Planning Board 
unanimously supported this.  It updates an existing bylaw that was designed to prevent the stripping of
land for sale outside of the town. The proposed change would allow the removal of certain things that 
cannot be reused after certain types of projects.
Motions & Debate
Motions were made and seconded for both recommendations for Favorable Action, and for Referral to 
the Planning Board.
Proponents of Favorable Action noted that the proposed changes have been reviewed by Town 
Counsel, the Planning Board, and CED. The changes make sense and are appropriate to update the 
existing bylaw.
Proponents of Referral to the Planning Board noted that, despite previous review, there was an error 
found [and updated], so some members questioned the need for additional review. Some members 
also noted that the subject matter could have been presented earlier in the meeting/hearing calendar, 
which would have increased the likelihood of catching errors and adjustments.
The committee voted 5-8-0 to reject the referral motion.
The committee voted 8-5-0 to recommend favorable action on the subject matter of Article 20. 
The committee voted 8-5-0 to recommend Favorable Action on the subject matter of Article 20.

Article 21 
Amend Zoning Bylaws: § V-G Flood
(Planning Board)
ARTICLE LANGUAGE
To see if the Town will vote to amend the Natick Zoning Bylaws by amending § V-G Flood; 
and further amend any other associated sections, where applicable; or otherwise act thereon.
PURPOSE OF THE ARTICLE
To amend the Natick Zoning Bylaws by amending § V-G Flood; and further amend any other 
associated sections, where applicable; or otherwise act thereon.
FINANCE COMMITTEE RECOMMENDATION
The Finance Committee
took the following action:
RECOMMENDATION: Refer to Sponsor
QUANTUM OF VOTE: 9-4-0
DATE VOTED: 9/30/2025
MOTION (Requires a 2/3rds Vote)
Move that the Town vote to amend the Natick Zoning Bylaws by deleting § V-G Flooding in its
entirety, and replace with “V-G RESERVED” to read as follows:
V-G. RESERVED
FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION
This motion was presented by Director of Community and Economic Development, Amanda 
Loomis. Ms. Loomis explained that the purpose of this motion is to delete a bylaw that is not 
currently being utilized and which would prohibit construction anywhere in Natick because of 
how broadly it is written. She noted that the Flood Plain bylaw and the Stormwater 
Management bylaw are intended to address the same concern. 
One Finance Committee member noted that zoning bylaws are written stating limits on what 
property owners can do on their property, but that the reason for such restrictions is to protect
abutting property owners. In response to a Finance Committee member question about how 
(if such bylaw were deleted)  a property owner would be protected against an abutting 
neighbor’s use of property subject to flooding in a manner as to endanger health or safety of 
94

--- Page 99 ---

the occupants, Ms  Loomis stated that if the abutting property was covered by the Stormwater
Management bylaw or was in a flood plain district, then Stormwater Management and/or 
Flood Plain bylaws would be the source of protection.
One Finance Committee member stated that if this bylaw is not currently being utilized, then 
deleting it should not change things for the Town. Other Finance Committee members 
expressed concern that the intent of the bylaw proposed to be deleted may not be fully 
addressed by the Stormwater Management bylaw and the Flood Plain district bylaw and that 
such deletion could leave people exposed whose properties are not in the designated district 
where the Stormwater Management bylaw applies or in a flood plain district. 
The committee voted 9-4-0 to recommend Referral to Sponsor on the subject matter of 
Article 21.
~~ END OF ARTICLE ~~

took the following action:

DATE VOTED: 9/30/2025
MOTION (Requires a 2/3rds Vote)
Move that the Town vote to amend Section 200 – Definitions of the Natick Zoning Bylaws, 
definition for Limited Site Plan Review by deleting the words “, or the expansion of existing 
structures, for the primary, accessory or incidental purpose of operating a child care facility” 
which appears after the words “No zoning bylaw in Natick shall prohibit, or require a special 
permit for, the use of land or structures” and appears before the words “; provided, however, 
that such lands or structures…” and replace with the words “for educational, religious, and 
child care uses, protected under Massachusetts General Law Chapter 40A Section 3 (the 
‘Dover Amendment’)” to read as follows:
Site Plan Review, Limited
: No zoning bylaw in Natick shall prohibit, or require a special 
permit for, the use of land or structures for educational, religious, and child care uses, 
protected under Massachusetts General Law Chapter 40A Section 3 (the ‘Dover 
Amendment’); provided, however, that such land or structures may be subject to reasonable 
regulations concerning the bulk and height of structures and determining yard sizes, lot area, 
setbacks, open space, parking and building coverage requirements. — MGL c. 40A, § 3, third 
para. (Art. 23, 2024 Spring ATM, 05/09/2024)
 .
96

--- Page 101 ---

FINANCE COMMITTEE PUBLIC HEARING AND DISCUSSION 
Ms. Loomis, Director of Community and Economic Development, presented this article. These 
changes are a requirement of the MA Attorney General for the Limited Site Plan Review bylaw, to 
clarify our compliance with the Dover Amendment.
Members reviewed the AG’s letter to the Town on this matter, and questioned if the AG’s opinion was 
a directive that changes are necessary, or if only recommended. The Sponsor indicated that the AG is 
requiring the changes, and that Town Counsel concurred. Subsequent to the Finance Committee 
hearing, Town Counsel affirmed that opinion.
Motions & Debate:
Motions were made and seconded for both a recommendation of Favorable Action, and for Referral to 
the Planning Board.
Members supporting Favorable Action noted that it’s the opinion of the Planning Board, CED, and 
Town Counsel that these changes are required by the AG’s office, and make sense for full compliance
with the Dover Amendment - which imposes limits on local review of certain projects brought forward 
by institution such as schools, religious organizations, qualified day cares, etc. 
Members supporting Referral, expressed uncertainty that the changes are really required;. A member 
also noted that the provisions related to day care had previously been in a different part of state law, 
and was unsure that they should be incorporated into these changes.
The committee voted 5-8-0 to reject the Referral motion.
The committee passed the Favorable Action motion by a vote of 8-5-0
The committee voted 8-5-0 to recommend Favorable Action on the subject matter of 
Article 22.
~~ END OF ARTICLE ~~

Article 23
Amend Zoning Bylaws: Use Regulation Schedule
(Planning Board)
ARTICLE LANGUAGE
To see if the Town will vote to amend the Natick Zoning Bylaws by amending § III-A.2 Use
Regulations Schedule (Use Categories within the Use Headers: G. Motor Vehicle Related 
Sales and Service Uses; H. Transportation, Communication, Utility Uses; and K. 
Manufacturing and Industrial Uses (amended to K. Light Manufacturing Uses; and N. 
Industrial Uses); amend Section 200 – Definitions; and further amend any other associated 
sections, where applicable; or otherwise act thereon.
PURPOSE OF THE ARTICLE
To amend the Natick Zoning Bylaws by amending § III-A.2 Use Regulations Schedule (Use 
Categories within the Use Headers: G. Motor Vehicle Related Sales and Service Uses; H. 
Transportation, Communication, Utility Uses; and K. Manufacturing and Industrial Uses 
(amended to K. Light Manufacturing Uses; and N. Industrial Uses); amend Section 200 – 
Definitions; and further amend any other associated sections, where applicable; or otherwise 
act thereon.

accessory structure.

: A parking garage for commercial use, which may

Parking Structure, or a Podium Parking Deck that includes parking spaces and 
adjacent access drives, aisles, and ramps that are located in a structure with one

totally below grade (underground) or either partially or totally above 
grade with those levels being either open or enclosed.
